7b Work With Us To Engage Your Offer In Compromise With The IRS Call (866) 675-7654

1bb Posted on September 2, 2010 by admin
92e


The IRS Form 656-B, Offer in Compromise Booklet has everything the taxpayer needs to engage an offer in compromise, including all worksheets and forms to correctly file your offer in compromise.

Taxpayers submitting there offer in compromise (OIC), must make sure that they are using the most current Form 656, Offer in Compromise or Form 656-L, Offer in Compromise (Doubt as to Liability) as these forms are updated regularly depending upon the premise for the filing of the Offer In Compromise. Taxpayers would fileForm 656 if there is even a chance that the tax liability would not be collected in a one time payment or an negotiated IRS repayment plan. The taxpayer should file Form 656-L if the tax liability is fraudulent or has been levied against the taxpayer in error.  Taxpayers can not claim that there tax liability was fraudulently entered against them and they also do not have the ability to pay it is either one or the other.

The taxpayer will be required, to submit Form 433-A, Collection Information Statement for Wage Earners and Self-Employed Individuals, and Form 433-B, Collection Information Statement if they own there own businesses.  If the taxpayer is claiming doubt as to liability these forms are not needed.

What are the Required Documents ?

All that is required is the “offer” which is cash and the 433-b or 433a. The Form 656-B has the Offer in Compromise Application Fee and Payment formula to determine the number of Forms 656 and applicable fees required to file the offer in compromise.

1b Offer In Compromise Formula 2b

186 Posted on January 23, 2009 by admin 20
23
645

According to IRS Doctrine from which the formula is engaged, a encompassing analysis of the taxpayers’ net present value, in addition to adequate consideration of the potential future income of the taxpayer. Right on the turn of the century, the IRS established a new amendment known as the deferred payment offer. The offer of a deferred payment when engaged allows the taxpayer to pay the present value of all assets in addition to a fee for the balance of the time for your collection due to the IRS.

Engagement of an offer of compromise, is first received by an IRS coordinator. The IRS coordinator preforms an examination to decide if the taxpayer is currently following all IRS guidelines and are currently in good standing with the IRS. After these prerequisites are met, the form is sent to the IRS Service Center for a second review of the tax history to figure out the exact tax liability which is due. The new offer can be rejected if the taxpayer has lied or has not followed IRS Doctrine.

(OIC) or Offer In Compromise is forwarded to an IRS Revenue Officer for an exhaustive review again. (OIC) or  Offer in Compromise Regulators do an investigation to determine if anything has been overlooked, The taxpayer may be interrogated by the IRS but this is very infrequent.

The IRS has three plans offered to taxpayers to submit their offer in compromise. The supply part of the offer in compromise can be paid within 90 days in full. The taxpayer must provide the (quick sale value) + total amount that the IRS can expect to collect over a period of 48 months

1d Offer In Compromise Worksheet 2b

188 Posted on January 23, 2009 by admin 20
23
49a

The reasonable accumulating total is the bulk of money the IRS thinks they can relieve from you for all of your tax debts. It is basically the defalcation amount of your assets plus your disposable assets over a season of 4 or 5 years.

Upon execution of your offer in compromise you must give the IRS in the debt instrument of your choice at least equal to what the IRS would collect from you over an extended period of time if you want the IRS to engage your offer in compromise.

The general rule of thumb is that if you have the ability to pay then you will not qualify for an offer in compromise and exercising this option will be a waste of time.

Basically the IRS takes these three things into consideration.

1. They will want all of your liquid cash, any amounts due you and any investments, stocks, or bonds
2. Then they will want the real value of any of your vehicles, real estate or anything else of value boats, go carts etc.
3. Also they will want your monthly disposable income over 60 months which is typically anything over 2,000 dollars for a single person or 2,500 for a married couple give or take 500 dollars.
